  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_62114f5f-dcf7-4f32-8d1e-ff7bf3f5166a'
      });

<div id="review_1354641145" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1354641145" />
    <a title="Gabrielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6753400-gabrielle"><img alt="Gabrielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598976963p2/6753400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1354641145?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabrielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabrielle" href="/user/show/6753400-gabrielle">Gabrielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=to-read-again">to-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=french">french</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=wwii">wwii</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=mandatory-reading">mandatory-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=own-a-copy">own-a-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1354641145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1088849075129058495">This book is thought-provoking and fascinating, and I can't say that I know how to start reviewing it. There are so many things to say about this book, and it made me feel a lot of strong emotions. Based on that alone, it should be obvious that I recommend it to everyone, but before you dive into it, you need to know what you are getting into, because this can be a very tough read at times.<br/><br/>This is at once a historical novel, and a clever work of speculative fiction, or alternate history. What if</span>
  <span id="freeText1088849075129058495" style="display:none">This book is thought-provoking and fascinating, and I can't say that I know how to start reviewing it. There are so many things to say about this book, and it made me feel a lot of strong emotions. Based on that alone, it should be obvious that I recommend it to everyone, but before you dive into it, you need to know what you are getting into, because this can be a very tough read at times.<br /><br />This is at once a historical novel, and a clever work of speculative fiction, or alternate history. What if Hitler had been accepted at the Fine Arts school in Vienna? What if he had travelled a bit, gotten to know all kinds of people, struggled with life in general, and art and relationships more specifically? Perhaps then he wouldn't have been the angry megalomaniac who perpetrated the horros of WWII.<br /><br />The narrative structure shows us two parallel stories: the historical version of what happened in Hitler's life, and the speculative version of what could have happened to a young man named Adolf H. Most people know the story of Hitler, his family background, his creative frustrations, his stint in the army during WWI, his eventual rise to power, the coup that he orchestrated to take charge of what he considered to be a weak government… and of course the ultimate dénoument: the Third Reich, the war and it's atrocities. There are retold here in vignettes, assuming the reader is well-informed. They are intertwined with another story: that of a young, struggling artist who is deadly intimidated by the nude models he must draw in class, who dreams of and eventually moves to Paris, to be part of the Montmartre art scene he has always wanted to be a part of. This young man meets love, looses it, lives on. What Schmitt shows the reader is the life of a perfectly normal man unfold before our eyes; what might have been.<br /><br />Certainly, Schmitt makes things relatively easy for Adolf H. He faces hurdles, but falls back on his feet pretty systematically. I think that while this might feel a little easy at times, when you look at the big picture of the work produced by Schmitt for this novel, I am happy to cut him some slack for having wished a good, happy life for his fictional character. But even despite the general fortunate life of Adolf H., the contrast to the historical reality creates a deep unease as the book progresses. Everyone knows how this story ends, but Schmitt keeps the reader on the edge of their seat until the last page.<br /><br />Which leads me to remark that this book is written with great compassion, and this might be the aspect fo it that moved me the most. Schmitt provides part of his reading journal at the end of the novel, to help the reader understand his process as he was writing, and in those notes he mentions how important it is to not dehumanize Hitler, who did terrible things because he unleashed the darkness within himself, but that we also can't forget that every human being has such darkness in them. The choices he made, how he reacted to the challenges he had to face: these are the things Schmitt wants to draw the reader's attention to, because that's where the root of how history unfolded lies. The potential to become Hitler is in every human being. The difference between him and Adolf H. is that the latter acknowledges his darkness and worked on himself.<br /><br />I mentionned before that I think Schmitt wanted his fictional character to be happy: through the historical chapters, at no point do we ever get the feeling that Hitler was in any way a happy man. There's no room for happiness when hatred and power are the only things that matter.<br /><br />A great, deeply disturbing, important novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1088849075129058495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <span id="freeText14724399254070107298" style="display:none">In theory it would have been a good idea to interweave two stories about the same person - one about the real personality of Hitler and one about how it could all have turned out if only Hitler had been accepted at the art school and become a famous painter. In my opinion, however, whereas the "real" Hitler is really well characterised and the true personality seems to pop out, the "good" Hitler is just overdone, I think. The book is well written, of course, but the "good" Hitler would have needed a little more work. Doesn't it seem a bit too simple that Hitler would have turned into a wonderful person if only he would have been accepted as a painter?</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer113322570&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer113322570" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"

<span id="freeTextContainer17832553065488670702">Wow. <br/><br/>When it comes to "evil" people - Hitler being the archetypal example - I have always felt strongly that "there but for the grace of God...", or "it could have been me (under other circumstances)". And that not only DO I recognize tendencies in myself that might lead to (great) evil, but that it is absolutely essential TO recognize such tendencies, rather than deny them or focus on how we are different from the "monsters". <br/><br/>Well, here's a book that speaks eloquently to those convictions, and </span>
  <span id="freeText17832553065488670702" style="display:none">Wow. <br /><br />When it comes to "evil" people - Hitler being the archetypal example - I have always felt strongly that "there but for the grace of God...", or "it could have been me (under other circumstances)". And that not only DO I recognize tendencies in myself that might lead to (great) evil, but that it is absolutely essential TO recognize such tendencies, rather than deny them or focus on how we are different from the "monsters". <br /><br />Well, here's a book that speaks eloquently to those convictions, and is very well-written and enjoyable to read to boot! I laughed out loud at some parts (the alternate-history Adolf H. in therapy chez Freud! no, I wouldn't have been able to resist that one either) and cringed or felt vaguely sickened at others (particularly when the author succeeds in making the young "real" Hitler recognizable enough; human enough). The author's notes at the end (included in this edition) were also quite thought-provoking.<br /><br />Very much recommended. It's been a good while since I enjoyed a book this much or that one stuck with me as long as I'm sure this one will. (I even conquered my general reluctance to read literary-level French to finish it in three days.)<br /><br />Possible caution: If you're disgusted by the very notion of trying to understand Hitler, or the idea of an alternate universe in which his life, and hence much of the 20th century, turned out quite differently... You should probably stay clear of this book. Unless of course you want a challenge.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17832553065488670702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2288103688" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2288103688" />
    <a title="GridGirl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65973916-gridgirl"><img alt="GridGirl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524235035p2/65973916.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2288103688?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="GridGirl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="GridGirl" href="/user/show/65973916-gridgirl">GridGirl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9783250601074" href="/book/show/2913060-adolf-h">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65973916-gridgirl?shelf=skoobe">skoobe</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2288103688" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6568430385131034237">I think the premise of this book is very thought-provoking and such an interesting concept. Hitler and the Third Reich are thoroughly discussed in German schools: History, German, English, Geography, Art – you name it. However, Hitler’s motivation is something that none of our teachers ever went into. One of the reasons for that might be that many things are unclear today and there are different theories for everything. This book explores one of many theories that might have led to Hitler being </span>
  <span id="freeText6568430385131034237" style="display:none">I think the premise of this book is very thought-provoking and such an interesting concept. Hitler and the Third Reich are thoroughly discussed in German schools: History, German, English, Geography, Art – you name it. However, Hitler’s motivation is something that none of our teachers ever went into. One of the reasons for that might be that many things are unclear today and there are different theories for everything. This book explores one of many theories that might have led to Hitler being who he was. This book was a great opportunity to engage in the person Hitler versus the historical and political consequences he initiated. However, this is still a work of fiction which means that the gaps between the known facts and figures are filled in by Schmitt’s imagination many times.<br />Overall, I enjoyed this book a lot and the story and the back and forth between the ‘real’ Hitler and Hitler, the famous painter, were very engaging. Nonetheless, the book felt like a somewhat slower read.<br /><br />4/5<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6568430385131034237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9454615954385557759" style="display:none">One of the best books I have read this year. It caught my attention by two different perspectives:<br />1. The psychological one, which emphasizes the importance of a single moment in our lives, of a single and apprently insignificant event in our lives. Not only the events are related breathtaking, but also Hitler's inner fight is amazingly explained. The book shows how important a family is, how important love in our lives is. And, of course, this books shows the importance of being aware of ourselves, of our flaws. And if we can not do that alone, then someone should help us getting over it.<br />2. The historical and political one, which gives you the opportunity to enter into the mind of one of the most powerful and controversial leaders of all time, which shows you how a problem can make one of the most dedicate leaders for their country into one of the dumbest and least open leaders to any other opinion.</span>

<div id="review_218599307" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/218599307" />
    <a title="Michel Bruneau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2981293-michel-bruneau"><img alt="Michel Bruneau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469061300p2/2981293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/218599307?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michel Bruneau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michel Bruneau" href="/user/show/2981293-michel-bruneau">Michel Bruneau</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218599307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5479047971195653853">The archetypal story of following the life that was and the life that could have been gets a news twist in this exploration of what Hitler's life could have been if a slightly different turn had been taken at a critical juncture. Quite a daring (near suicidal) proposition for a writer, but Schmitt pulls it off, with a successful balancing act of fact and fiction. An introspection that leaves the reader wondering if there could be a little bit (or a lot) of Hitler in any human being, ready to be </span>
  <span id="freeText5479047971195653853" style="display:none">The archetypal story of following the life that was and the life that could have been gets a news twist in this exploration of what Hitler's life could have been if a slightly different turn had been taken at a critical juncture. Quite a daring (near suicidal) proposition for a writer, but Schmitt pulls it off, with a successful balancing act of fact and fiction. An introspection that leaves the reader wondering if there could be a little bit (or a lot) of Hitler in any human being, ready to be unleashed, triggered by an unfortunate event, just like a butterfly effect that can trigger a hurricane.<br /><br />Note: The English version of this book (according to <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89ric-Emmanuel_Schmitt">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89ri...</a>) is "The Alternative Hypothesis (not found on Amazon.com).</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2615534937" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2615534937" />
    <a title="Ivaylo Yorgov" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22895573-ivaylo-yorgov"><img alt="Ivaylo Yorgov" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

<div id="review_2581153647" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2581153647" />
    <a title="Linh Nguyen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63404107-linh-nguyen"><img alt="Linh Nguyen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589102739p2/63404107.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2581153647?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linh Nguyen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linh Nguyen" href="/user/show/63404107-linh-nguyen">Linh Nguyen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/13257389-n-a-kia-c-a-hitler">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2581153647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4833896327429305230">I like everything he wrote about the making of Hitler, how his character developed, how increasingly fanatical he became and what drove him to the point of insanity.<br/>I like how at the starting point, both Hitler and Adolf H. are the same person with the same personality (idealistic, a bit extreme, over confident, anger issue, etc.) and I like how they encounter almost every major events in their lives similarly (two wars, mental health, childhood traumas) but wound up to be two very different peo</span>
  <span id="freeText4833896327429305230" style="display:none">I like everything he wrote about the making of Hitler, how his character developed, how increasingly fanatical he became and what drove him to the point of insanity.<br />I like how at the starting point, both Hitler and Adolf H. are the same person with the same personality (idealistic, a bit extreme, over confident, anger issue, etc.) and I like how they encounter almost every major events in their lives similarly (two wars, mental health, childhood traumas) but wound up to be two very different people. That goes to show how a person’s destiny could be largely shaped from their surroundings and environment. Especially the point of fame: Hitler became obsessed and idolized himself to be some sort of God sent savior and the center of the universe, while Adolf H. gained fame from actual talent but went on to almost reject the fame and chose to live ordinary and happy (I hope).<br />I like the touch on mental health to show the importance of knowing about mental illness and get proper help.<br />I like the bit about the last days of Hitler and how his body deteriorated as he strayed further from sanity (could just be a product of his mind though).<br />But, while Hitler was depicted clearly, Adolf H. is almost redundant at times. His character development is not exactly linear and the people in his life were both important to the developing of him as a person but also at times felt like the author wasn’t exactly sure of their roles in the story overall. I just wish I like Adolf H. enough but unfortunately I don’t.<br />However, the story ends with an epilogue from the author, saying that Hitler is “not much different from you or me”, and I think it’s a very sharp conclusion to draw from the book. That one mindless wrong step could lead to the doom of a generation and one right step could potentially change the course of the world, to remind you to be good, be humble, to be conscious of your decisions.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4833896327429305230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14870634552002703941" style="display:none">Just finished the last fifty or so pages of this book. It took me a little while to finish this but it was all due to lack of time or fatigue, it had nothing to do with the book itself. <br /><br />I found it very interesting to read about the man that was Hitler and realize that he was in fact really crazy. He seemed to really believe in what he was doing. I don't know how to describe it but he was quite different from what I imagined. Also his relationship with Eva Braun is show in a totally different light here, I mean, wow. Poor girl. Delusional girl. <br /><br />Adolf H., his other self, was basically the same person to start with. I didn't like him in the first forty or so years of his life, really. At the end he somehow grew on me a bit but generally this is not a character who I could call one of my favourites. Still better than the original though.<br /><br />I thought it interesting to see how one circumstance, one situation, could change the course of a person's life so drastically. All one can really hope for in life, is that it gives us a break so we don't go around starting wars that kill millions of people :P</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('U0ER2GylWmAme2RV6ybUuCcCmpicg+f8eR07Q74FVKGnphlz3O+MHKLIrheUsJB32ZZvT5VilN+geP/FAFJgSA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('U4ZSeYf0XY6hoKG7/jHRDqTUK0sors1p5M8IwmWcMjCnYVrSN76L8iUTa/mBp5XBWkDenCFPvko9qsxE28sG2Q==')})
  }

//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_990579'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/990579.Chercher_le_vent?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Chercher le vent<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/498585.Guillaume_Vigneault?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Guillaume Vigneault<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.79 avg rating &mdash; 858 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2001\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer3157902903494772063\">Décidément, Guillaume Vigneault a de qui tenir. Le fils du célèbre chanteur et poète n\'a pas tardé à se faire un prénom. Son second roman confirme le talent révélé par le premier, Carnets de naufrage. Comme ce dernier, Chercher le vent dépeint avec j<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText3157902903494772063\" style=\"display:none\">Décidément, Guillaume Vigneault a de qui tenir. Le fils du célèbre chanteur et poète n\'a pas tardé à se faire un prénom. Son second roman confirme le talent révélé par le premier, Carnets de naufrage. Comme ce dernier, Chercher le vent dépeint avec justesse un jeune homme aux prises avec une crise amoureuse et existentielle, et nous plonge dans un univers mâle sensible qui réconcilie action et introspection. Vigneault a ici une manière très contemporaine d\'interroger l\'amitié masculine et la complexité de l\'amour.  Menée par une écriture séduisante, simple mais imagée, où pointe un sens de la formule ironique (La douche est à l\'infidélité ce que le maquillage mortuaire est au cadavre : un touchant effort), l\'histoire nous propulse sur les pas de Jack, qui se sent comme une coquille vide depuis que sa femme l\'a quitté. Le narrateur de 36 ans a abandonné toutes ses passions : l\'aviation, le surf, son métier de photographe. Il se laisse pourtant entraîner aux États-Unis par Tristan, son ex-beau-frère, un excessif souffrant de maniaco-dépression. En chemin, le duo prend une auto-stoppeuse qui devient bientôt la maîtresse de Tristan. La belle Nuna en pince plutôt pour Jack, mais il faudra d\'abord que celui-ci accepte de se pardonner pour reprendre le risque de l\'amour…  Véritable road book pétri d\'américanité (le prénom du narrateur évoque à la fois Sur la route de Jack Kerouac et Volkswagen Blues de Jacques Poulin), Chercher le vent nous promène de Floride en Louisiane, où notre héros devra affronter une nature déchaînée. Un voyage rédempteur pour Jack, et très attrayant pour le lecteur. --Marie Labrecque<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"3157902903494772063\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return Patrick Senécal est en effet passé maître dans l\'art d\'aspirer son lecteur dans la spirale infernale de l\'étrange. Inexorablement.  Étienne Séguin vit à Montréal. Sa femme l\'a quitté et ce jeune homme sensible a du mal à croire qu\'il se remettra un jour de ce gros chagrin d\'amour. Quand on lui offre un poste de professeur de littérature à Drummondville, sa ville natale, il accepte sans hésiter, voyant là une occasion unique de se changer les idées. Il devra y enseigner le roman fantastique, lui qui n\'a, dit-il, jamais été attiré par la violence.  Trois fois par semaine, le jeune prof emprunte l\'autoroute 20, entre Montréal et Drummondville. Sans savoir pourquoi, il est irrésistiblement attiré par un auto-stoppeur, posté toujours au même endroit, toujours à la même heure. Il finit par s\'arrêter et comprend vite que ce passager n\'est pas un étranger, mais qu\'il l\'a connu, enfant, avant qu\'un coup reçu sur la tête le plonge dans une amnésie totale. (…) pendant quelques secondes, sa silhouette se découpe à contre-jour de façon plutôt impressionnante, telle une entité mystérieuse émergeant des ténèbres. Je me dis même tout à coup que j\'ai fait une erreur, que je devrais partir tout de suite… Évidemment, Étienne ne partira pas et découvrira, à l\'issue d\'un véritable voyage au bout de l\'enfer, une part de lui-même engloutie dans un lointain passé.  L\'auteur des Sept Jours du talion maîtrise sur le bout des doigts la partition de l\'horreur. Suspense, action, amnésie, cauchemars récurrents, fausses coïncidences, lieux déserts, Senécal exploite tous les rouages du genre avec la dextérité d\'un pianiste effréné. Dans une langue sans grand effet de style, mais d\'une redoutable efficacité, l\'un des rares auteurs québécois de roman noir prend son lecteur au piège, comme son héros, et ne les lâche que quand Mais derrière cette douleur s’en cache une autre, plus profonde encore: celle créée par son père, le jour où il a quitté sa famille pour refaire sa vie. Émilie aimerait se reconstruire, mais les morceaux sont petits et le casse-tête, interminable.\n\nEn apparence, Émilie et Jake n’ont rien en commun, sauf leurs blessures béantes au cœur et leur travail à la pizzéria du coin.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2976._ric_Emmanuel_Schmitt">About Éric-Emmanuel Schmitt</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2976._ric_Emmanuel_Schmitt"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1256959070p3/2976.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/2976._ric_Emmanuel_Schmitt">Éric-Emmanuel Schmitt
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,803
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8909335208858460988">A popular contemporary French author and dramatist, his plays are translated and staged in more than 30 countries all over the world.<br/><br/>He studied at the Lycée du Parc in Lyon and was accepted at the famous École normale supérieure in Paris (1980–1985), where he received a doctorate in philosophy. As the theme for his dissertation, he chose "Diderot and metaphysics". He spent three years teaching in </span>
  <span id="freeText8909335208858460988" style="display:none">A popular contemporary French author and dramatist, his plays are translated and staged in more than 30 countries all over the world.<br /><br />He studied at the Lycée du Parc in Lyon and was accepted at the famous École normale supérieure in Paris (1980–1985), where he received a doctorate in philosophy. As the theme for his dissertation, he chose "Diderot and metaphysics". He spent three years teaching in Cherbourg and at the university of Chambéry.<br /><br />He is of Alsation extraction. Both of his parents were physical education teachers. Growing up under the influence of his parents' atheist outlook, Schmitt eventually professed himself a Christian, after years of being an agnostic.<br /><br />Initially he became known as a scriptwriter for the stage. His debut work, "La nuit de Valognes", was produced a number of times in 1991/1992, both in France and abroad. His breakthrough theatre work came with his second script, "Le Visiteur", which won Molière prizes for best author and best show in 1993.<br /><br />The following years were littered with theatrical successes such as "Golden Joe" (1995), "Variations Énigmatiques" (1996), "Le Libertin" (1997), "Milarepa" (1997), "Frédérick ou Le Boulevard du Crime" (1998), "Hôtel des deux mondes" (1999) and "Monsieur Ibrahim et les fleurs du Coran" (1999).<br /><br />Schmitt covers a variety of themes in his work. "Golden Joe" takes a look of the cynical attitudes to life of those involved in high finance. In "Variations énigmatiques", the author gives voice to two very different men, who discuss their own philosophies of life and love - as it turns out, both were in love with the same woman. "Le Libertin" is a historical drama about the life of philosopher Denis Diderot and a film version was released in 2000.<br /><br />In 2001, Schmitt was awarded the "Grand Prix du théâtre de l'Académie Française". His plays have been performed in 35 countries and translated into many languages. They show influences from Samuel Beckett, Jean Anouilh and Paul Claudel, among others.<br /><br />In addition to his plays, Schmitt has written a number of successful novels, including "La Secte des Égoïstes" (1994), "Oscar et la dame rose" (1999), "L'Évangile selon Pilate" (2000), "La Part de l'Autre" (2001), "Lorsque j'étais une œuvre d'art" (2002), "L'enfant de Noé" (2004), "Ma vie avec Mozart" (2005).<br /><br />World religions play an important role in Schmitt's writing. In "Le Cycle de l'Invisible", Schmitt attempts a harmonization of religions and cultures. "Milarepa" is the first issue in this series and depicts Tibetan Buddhism. The second volume, "Monsieur Ibrahim et les fleurs du Coran" is dedicated to Sufism, a subset of Islam, also referencing Judaism. "Oscar et la dame rose" (the third volume) concerns Christianity. "L'enfant de Noé" (a comparison of Judaism and Christianity) rounds off the series.<br /><br />"Monsieur Ibrahim et les fleurs du Coran" (English: M. Ibrahim and the Flowers of the Koran) received the German prize for fiction in 2004 and a film version was produced in 2003, directed by François Dupeyron with Omar Sharif in the title role.<br /><br />Persian:<br />اریک امانوئل شمیت </span>
  <a data-text-id="8909335208858460988" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1153095-la-part-de-l-autre">Quotes from La Part de l&#39;autre</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Mes amis, j'écris ce petit mot pour vous dire que je vous aime, que je pars avec la fierté de vous avoir connus, l'orgueil d'avoir été choisi et apprécié par vous, et que notre amitié fut sans doute la plus belle œuvre de ma vie. C'est étrange, l'amitié. Alors qu'en amour, on parle d'amour, entre vrais amis on ne parle pas d'amitié. L'amitié, on la fait sans la nommer ni la commenter. C'est fort et silencieux. C'est pudique. C'est viril. C'est le romantisme des hommes. Elle doit être beaucoup plus profonde et solide que l'amour pour qu'on ne la disperse pas sottement en mots, en déclarations, en poèmes, en lettres. Elle doit être beaucoup plus satisfaisante que le sexe puisqu'elle ne se confond pas avec le plaisir et les démangeaisons de peau. En mourant, c'est à ce grand mystère silencieux que je songe et je lui rends hommage.<br />Mes amis, je vous ai vus mal rasés, crottés, de mauvaise humeur, en train de vous gratter, de péter, de roter, et pourtant je n'ai jamais cessé de vous aimer. J'en aurais sans doute voulu à une femme de m'imposer toutes ses misères, je l'aurais quittée, insultée, répudiée. Vous pas. Au contraire. Chaque fois que je vous voyais plus vulnérables, je vous aimais davantage. C'est injuste n'est-ce pas? L'homme et la femme ne s'aimeront jamais aussi authentiquement que deux amis parce que leur relation est pourrie par la séduction. Ils jouent un rôle. Pire, ils cherchent chacun le beau rôle. Théâtre. Comédie. Mensonge. Il n'y a pas de sécurité en l'amour car chacun pense qu'il doit dissimuler, qu'il ne peut être aimé tel qu'il est. Apparence. Fausse façade. Un grand amour, c'est un mensonge réussi et constamment renouvelé. Une amitié, c'est une vérité qui s'impose. L'amitié est nue, l'amour fardé.<br />Mes amis, je vous aime donc tels que vous êtes.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/871655-mes-amis-j-cris-ce-petit-mot-pour-vous-dire-que">9 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Un homme est fait de choix et de circonstances. Personne n'a de pouvoir sur les circonstances, mais chacun en a sur ses choix.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/9325014-un-homme-est-fait-de-choix-et-de-circonstances-personne">2 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/1153095-la-part-de-l-autre">More quotes&hellip;</a>

a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.

last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
React component will render its content.
-->
